Saturday, 12:16 p.m. – You've Got to Flight for Your Right to Party
-------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Event Coverage team*

European Grand Prix being what they are, there is a very real chance that one will find oneself having to battle through an inordinate number of rounds to make it into the prizes. While Grand Prix Brussels has tipped the scales at a mere 1,667 players (still the biggest Standard tournament ever) having 3 byes is something that most would aspire to, even if few achieve it.


The pros are rightly resting n the laurels of past successes for the first 3 rounds today, as are those who were able to win through in a Grand Prix Trial. The last of these trials came in 20 flights on Friday. These tournaments would be a last chance to hone decks, and win a few precious byes in the event.


Many might have predicted such a string of tournaments would be a bit of a Jundfest. While there were plenty of copies of the deck being played, only 6 scored the byes. In fact the metagame of winners is stunningly diverse. If you are looking for some fun decks to play in standard, you could do a lot worse than scrolling down right now.







#### Stijn van Gethem


#####

**Don Mysterioso\***


*Grand Prix Brussels 2010 Trials - Flight 20*

Podcast - Friday on Saturday
----------------------------


*by Rich Hagon*


Here's what you normally do on a Euro Grand Prix Friday: Fly to host country. Travel to venue. Register. Eat. Go to bed. Here's what you do at GP Brussels 2010 on Friday: Fly to host country. Travel to venue. Play a GP Trial. Have lunch. Play in up to four more out of twenty GP Trials. Have some food. Register. Eat. Play in Super Friday Night Magic. Win stuff. Realize just how much you love this game. Go to bed...Tall tales from Super [FNM](http://archive.wizards.com/Magic/Magazine/Article.aspx?x=events/magic/fnm) and the juicy goodness of twenty Trial-winning decklists kick off our monster weekend of Standard shenanigans.


[Download MP3](http://webcast2.wizards.com/podcasts/10brussels/GP%20Brussels%201.mp3)


 

Saturday, 1:00 p.m. –
---------------------


*by David Sutcliffe*

I have a confession to make.


I had never played Friday Night Magic before last night.


There. It's out now. The world knows. I had never played Friday Night Magic. It's not that I've been avoiding them, don't get me wrong. I love the idea of Friday Night Magic, but I've just never found myself in a games store on a Friday night with a Magic deck and ready to play. But at Grand Prix Brussels that was about to change. For the first time in Europe the Grand Prix hall was open the day (and night) before the Grand Prix began and while dozens of Grand Prix Trial flights were running on one side of the room, the other side of the room was going to be dedicated to a "Super Friday Night Magic" tournament.


So. I was here. It was a Friday night. It was a Magic tournament. Oh, but I still did't have a deck with me.


What's that? It's a Sealed Deck [FNM](http://archive.wizards.com/Magic/Magazine/Article.aspx?x=events/magic/fnm)?


Well... it looked like I was out of excuses then, didn't it?


I handed over my DCI number and took my seat. The boosters were handed out and I hurriedly tore open the first one, instantly flicking past all the commons and uncommons to see what rare I had got... [Day of Judgment](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Day+of+Judgment). I smiled. I was going to like [FNM](http://archive.wizards.com/Magic/Magazine/Article.aspx?x=events/magic/fnm).

LAND
 1 [Magosi, The Waterveil](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Magosi%2C+The+Waterveil)
 1 [Piranha Marsh](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Piranha+Marsh) |

It wasn't hard to spot the standout cards in this pool...


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration//mtg/images/daily/events/gpbru10/fnm_rares.jpg)*LOOK AT THOSE RARES! Woooooo!*
I would need a very compelling reason not to play a blue-white deck after that. In white I had a slew of good removal cards that were pretty much too good to ignore - [Day of Judgment](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Day+of+Judgment) was obviously the highlight but there was also [Pitfall Trap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pitfall+Trap), [Journey to Nowhere](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Journey+to+Nowhere), [Arrow Volley Trap](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arrow+Volley+Trap), and Iona's Judgment, and also some of the best creatures in my pool with [Shepherd of the Lost](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shepherd+of+the+Lost) and the great utility of [Kor Sanctifiers](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kor+Sanctifiers) - a card I would almost always be happy to see during a game. Outside of [Sphinx of Jwar Isle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sphinx+of+Jwar+Isle) and [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Jace%2C+the+Mind+Sculptor) my blue cards weren't too thrilling, but they still offered some good cheap creatures like [Sejiri Merfolk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sejiri+Merfolk), [Welkin Tern](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Welkin+Tern), and [Wind Zendikon](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wind+Zendikon). Hardly the most exciting bunch of cards, but could I really ignore [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Jace%252C%2Bthe%2BMind%2BSculptor) and the Sphinx?


Looking at the black cards I could see that I had a few good removal cards, like [Gatekeeper of Malakir](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gatekeeper+of+Malakir), [Tomb Hex](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tomb+Hex), and [Heartstabber Mosquito](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Heartstabber+Mosquito) and with a few solid creatures like [Ruthless Cullblade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ruthless+Cullblade) and [Crypt Ripper](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crypt+Ripper) - it was a viable option but didn't offer anything of the power level of blue, or the depth of good cards in white. The red cards were similar, with a couple of nice removal spells and a couple of decent creatures , and the green was... well... there were some green cards.


Settling on blue-white I pulled the deck together, but a problem was immediately apparent. After [Sphinx of Jwar Isle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sphinx+of+Jwar+Isle) and [Shepherd of the Lost](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shepherd+of+the+Lost)s my next best creature was.... [Battle Hurda](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Battle+Hurda)? And after that... [Sejiri Merfolk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sejiri+Merfolk)? And as well as not having a lot of good creatures I didn't have a lot of creatures, period, and I was having to play some blue counterspells just to make the deck up to 40 cards. I was struggling to see how I could win a game if I somehow lost the Sphinx and the Shepherd so decided at the last minute to include a black splash for one spell - Grim Recovery. Having a [Raise Dead](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Raise+Dead) in my deck would mean that my Sphinx could return for revenge should something happen to him first time round.


I guess I could always use [Jace, the Mind Sculptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?&name=Jace%252C%2Bthe%2BMind%2BSculptor)'s ultimate ability to win a game though. Yeah... right.
